First off, I''d like to say the User Guide is really bad for the free version. The video goes into how to customize your experience while using the enhanced version, which has some QOL features not present in the free template. This has thrown me off, because of how quick and easy it is to create the downstream from goals in the video (literally one click - that do not work on the free version) to how annoying it becomes in the free version. Furthermore, you just hint on the video how to do it in the free version, instead of actually walking through - which would be very helpful. 

Second, the lack of a dashboard/homepage is really offputting. We should have a dashboard with user level and tasks + daily quests as the homepage (with both store and badges). This way we can quickly overlook what is to be done on a daily basis, instead of having to go under your user to start using it. A dashboard/homepage would be much more welcoming for new users, giving a good "HUD" for the day-to-day tasks we need to perform. This could also be paired with a starting theme - nothing too big, just something to make the page look more like a game, instead of a blog post.

I understand the need to create a paid version - you have put a lot of work into this and there should be no shame in monetizing your work. However, monetizing key features for the functioning of the ''game'', in other words, transforming what is advertised as ''free'' into pay-to-win, is a sure way of keeping new players away from experimenting. My first problem, as I previously said, was with the difficulties of creating downstream tasks from goals, but afterward it is also a concern that not having a store would make collecting gold kind of pointless. On top of that, the lack of badges is also pretty upsetting, since this would be a garanteed way of keeping people on track with their goals. I believe all of those features should be F2P, as they seem - to me at least - like the core features of gamification. 

Of course this comes down to your business model, wheter you want to appeal only to notion geeks or if you have a larger audience in mind. There''s no problem with a targeted audience, mind you, I just wanted to point out some changes that could make more people jump into the free version of your project. On the question of monetization, maybe the release of themed templates, exclusive badges and hell, even tutorials, could be the way to go. Who knows, maybe even releasing the full enhanced version for free and allowing the influx of people to cover this on patreon could work - although it might very well not work. 

Lastly, I just wanted to congratulate you on creating the best gamification tool I''ve seen out there. Habitica isn''t anywhere near as useful as your project seems to be, it''s just a shame that the free version lacks some core features to be fully useful.  (the 1 star reflects that I''m not using the free version, not that the tool itself is bad by any means).

Regardless, I wish you all the best, hopefully this expands to be the biggest notion template out there, and who knows, maybe even the bigger gamification tool!
